IMPORTS
    MODULE-IDENTITY, OBJECT-TYPE, Integer32, NOTIFICATION-TYPE, enterprises        FROM SNMPv2-SMI
    DisplayString, RowStatus                                                                                     FROM SNMPv2-TC
    senProducts                                                                                                        FROM SEN-ROOT-MIB;

        ansible                OBJECT IDENTIFIER ::= { senProducts 6 }
                                -- Ansible product-specific MIBs
                                --                = senProducts         6
                                --                = enterprises sen   1 6
                                --                = enterprises 32804 1 6
                                --                = 1 3 6 1 4 1 32804 1 6

        
        alarms                MODULE-IDENTITY
        LAST-UPDATED        "201409150000Z"
        ORGANIZATION        "Unify"
        CONTACT-INFO        "Uwe Grothe
                                        Postal:        5500 Broken Sound Blvd NW
                                                        Boca Raton, FL 33487-3501                                                
                                        E-mail:        uwe.grothe@unify.com"

        DESCRIPTION        "This MIB module implements SNMP Alarms.
                            An alarm is uniquely identified by the trap name
                            (mainly the last two numbers of the trap OID)
                            and the neName.
                            An alarm trap is a trap with a non-cleared severity.
                            It is cleared by the same trap
                            with the same neName and a severity of clear.
                            An existing alarm can be modified by a trap with the
                            same OID and neName but with one or more modified values,
                            e.g. for severity, nodes, or faultyObject"

        ::= { ansible 1 }

        trapParameters              OBJECT IDENTIFIER ::= { alarms 1 }
        eventCommon                 OBJECT IDENTIFIER ::= { alarms 2 }
        eventGroups                 OBJECT IDENTIFIER ::= { alarms 3 }
        eventGroupsC                OBJECT IDENTIFIER ::= { alarms 4 }

        eventGroup01                OBJECT IDENTIFIER ::= { eventGroups  1 }

        --********************************************************************
        -- Alarm Trap Parameters:
        --********************************************************************

        neName                     OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     DisplayString
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "name of the network element sending the alarm"
        ::= { trapParameters 1 }


        neType                     OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     DisplayString
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "Indicate the network element type"
        ::= { trapParameters 2 }

   
        eventGroupName             OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     DisplayString
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "corresponds to the eventGroup, 
                                    the second last number of the trap OID."
        ::= { trapParameters 3 }


        eventName                  OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     DisplayString
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "corresponds to the event within the eventGroup
                                    reported by the trap, the last number of the trap OID."
        ::= { trapParameters 4 }


        correlationId              OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     DisplayString
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "same value for traps associated with the same active alarm."
        ::= { trapParameters 5 }


        severity                   OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     INTEGER        {indeterminate(0),   -- not used
                                        critical(1),
                                        major(2),
                                        minor(3),
                                        warning(4),                    -- not used
                                        cleared(5) }
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "corresponds to X.721/X.733:PerceivedSeverity.
                                    indeterminate and warning are not used.
                                    critical, major, ,and minor correspond to an alarm.
                                    cleared corresponds to an alarm clearance event, which clears
                                    all alarms of the network element that 
                                    had been reported by this trap."
        ::= { trapParameters 6 }

     
        eventTime                  OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     DisplayString
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "An element of X.710: Parameter contains
                                    the time of generation of the event,
                                    The EventTime is a GeneralizedTime (defined in X.208),
                                    format is YYYYMMDDhhmmss.f+hhmm where 
                                    Y year 
                                    M month in year
                                    D day in month
                                    h hour in day (0-23)
                                    m minute in hour
                                    s second in minute
                                    f tenth part of second
                                    +hhmm        local time offset(+-) to UTC time. 
                                    Time represents the local time (t1), and the time 
                                    differential (t2) enables UTC time to be determined as follows:
                                    UTC time = t1 - t2"
        ::= { trapParameters 7 } 


        nodes                      OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     DisplayString
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "comma delimited list of node names associated with the alarm"
        ::= { trapParameters 8 }


        faultyObject               OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     DisplayString
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "Specifies the component of the network element at fault."
        ::= { trapParameters 9 }
  

        monitoredValue             OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     DisplayString
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "Specifies the value of the current condition of the system
                                    for this particular alarm"
        ::= { trapParameters 10 }


        thresholdValues            OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     DisplayString
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "Specifies the values that needs to be crossed by
                                    monitored-value for an alarm to be generated.
                                    Up to 3 values separated by comma can be defined
                                    associated with the severities minor,major,critical.
                                    e.g. ,3,8 means major alarm when monitored value is 3 or higher
                                    and critical alarm when 8 or higher. No minor alarm"
        ::= { trapParameters 11 }


        info                       OBJECT-TYPE
        SYNTAX                     DisplayString
        MAX-ACCESS                 not-accessible
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "Indicate the network element type"
        ::= { trapParameters 12 }


        --********************************************************************
        -- Common Trap Definitions
        --********************************************************************


        networkElementStarting     NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventTime }
        STATUS                     current
        DESCRIPTION                "This trap reports that the network element is starting up.
                                    All alarms of this network element shall be deleted."
        ::= { eventCommon 1 }

        --********************************************************************
        -- Alarm Trap Definitions for alarms sent by a particular node
        -- (using eventGroup)
        --********************************************************************

        --********************************************************************
        -- Alarm Trap Definitions for event group 01: Platform
        --********************************************************************

        alarm01001 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 01: Platform
                                eventName,                             -- 001: InvalidAlarmConfiguration
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            The alarm configuration has problems.
                            Check the problem listed in the faulty object and correct."
        ::= { eventGroup01 1 }

        alarm01002 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 01: Platform
                                eventName,                             -- 002: InvalidTimezoneConfiguration
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            The timezone configured in the datacenter configuration in the ZooKeeper database is not one of values supported by the Linux Operating System. An invalid timezone will be ignored so the timezone will remain as the default timezone (UTC) or the last valid timezone that was successfully configured.
                            Manually change the timezone in the datacenter configuration in the ZooKeeper database to a valid timezone. Valid timezones can be found under directory /usr/share/zoneinfo (e.g. US/Eastern)."
        ::= { eventGroup01 2 }

        alarm01003 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 01: Platform
                                eventName,                             -- 003: UnknownAlarmId
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            An alarm has been raised or used with an unknown group ID and/or event ID.
                            Check if the alarm should be raised/used. If correct, add alarm to alarm configuration."
        ::= { eventGroup01 3 }

        alarm01004 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 01: Platform
                                eventName,                             -- 004: InvalidMonitoredValue
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            An alarm has been raised or used with an invalid monitored attribute value.
                            Correct code raising the alarm."
        ::= { eventGroup01 4 }

        alarm01005 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 01: Platform
                                eventName,                             -- 005: FaultyObjectTooLong
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            An alarm has been raised with a FaultyObject string that is longer than 255. It has been truncated.
                            Correct code raising the alarm."
        ::= { eventGroup01 5 }

        alarm01006 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 01: Platform
                                eventName,                             -- 006: AddlInfoTooLong
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            An alarm has been raised with an Addl Info string that is longer than 255. It has been truncated.
                            Correct code raising the alarm."
        ::= { eventGroup01 6 }

        alarm01007 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 01: Platform
                                eventName,                             -- 007: TooManyAlarmParameters
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            There is additional text after AddlInfo in the reported alarm string.
                            Correct code raising the alarm."
        ::= { eventGroup01 7 }


        --********************************************************************
        -- Alarm Trap Definitions for event group 03: FileTransfer
        --********************************************************************

        alarm03001 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 03: FileTransfer
                                eventName,                             -- 001: ExportFailing
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            The SFTP connection to remote server has failed for this instance.
                            Probably due to bad File Export configuration data or a network issue where we cannot communicate with the SFTP server. Please check /var/log/platform/logging/LogIssues.log file. Collect the output of the command /opt/platform/bin/plat_fe_ctl --display_working_config."
        ::= { eventGroup03 1 }

        alarm03002 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 03: FileTransfer
                                eventName,                             -- 002: ExportFailing

                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current

        --********************************************************************
        -- Alarm Trap Definitions for event group 04: Process
        --********************************************************************

        alarm04001 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 04: Process
                                eventName,                             -- 001: PmAborted
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            Process Monitoring has aborted.
                            Check configuration files and get logs in debug level 7."
        ::= { eventGroup04 1 }

        alarm04002 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 04: Process
                                eventName,                             -- 002: NetworkNotRunning
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            The node process manager has found that the process/application is not running. It either could not be started during startup or it failed during normal operation. Usually the process is restarted automatically. In some cases the problem might even escalate to a full node restart.
                            The alarm is cleared if PM was able to start the process.
If the alarm is still active or if the alarm has been reported many times the issue should be escalated to development for SW debugging.
Navigate to the log manager GUI and run debug file collection for the node.
Attach the collected debug file to the fault report."
        ::= { eventGroup04 2 }

        alarm04003 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 04: Process
                                eventName,                             -- 003: RoutesNotRunning
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            The node process manager has found that the process/application is not running. It either could not be started during startup or it failed during normal operation. Usually the process is restarted automatically. In some cases the problem might even escalate to a full node restart.

        alarm05001 NOTIFICATION-TYPE

                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 05: ProcessManager
                                eventName,                             -- 001: InvalidPlatConfiguration
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            Platform configuration has invalid parameters:
A failure type of 1 means a missing or wrong configuration. PM can run.
2 means missing or wrong process configuration. PM can run but a process has potential problems.
3 means that the configuration file was rejected.
                            Check faulty object to know where the problem is located."
        ::= { eventGroup05 1 }

        alarm05003 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 05: ProcessManager
                                eventName,                             -- 003: CanNotExecuteCommand
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,

                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            One command could not be executed:
Command capabilities = 2 means that the command is important for PM operation and 3 means that it affects node operation.
                            Check faulty object and try to execute it by hand."
        ::= { eventGroup05 3 }

        alarm05004 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 05: ProcessManager
                                eventName,                             -- 004: UnexpectedBehaviour
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            PM has found an unexpected behavior during its execution.
1 means that PM is still running and only a feature affected.
2 means that PM is still running, but that process control is affected.
3 means that PM will abort and restart.
                            Check faulty object for function name and line number of the problem."
        ::= { eventGroup05 4 }

        alarm05005 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 05: ProcessManager
                                eventName,                             -- 005: RecoverEscalation
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            One or more process cannot be started.
If server Health State is 1 and the process continues to fail, all applicaton processes (Lvl 3) will be restarted.
If the HealthState is 2, the application restart did not work and all platform and all application processes (Lvl 1 and 2 will be restarted.
If the HealthState is 3, the node will be rebooted within 5 minutes.
                            Check which processe(s) are not working. Look for alarms reporting pstacks and coredumps. Collect debug files and send them to the next level of support for analysis."
        ::= { eventGroup05 5 }


        --********************************************************************
        -- Alarm Trap Definitions for event group 06: CoreDump
        --********************************************************************

        alarm06001 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 06: CoreDump
                                eventName,                             -- 001: PstackFound1
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            A pstack has been found. There was a severe SW error within the process/application specified in the faultyObject. Debugging information has been stored in the pstack file. Usually the faulty process recovers from the error, but it could also be that some features may not work properly. A continuous process failure may also escalate to a node restart.
The alarm is auto-deleted after some hours unless it is overwritten by a more recent core dump.
                            The problem can only be repaired by a SW correction. In order to collect debug information navigate to the log manager GUI and sort through the file collection directory for pstack files based on time stamp and process name. Upload the file.
Also run debug file collection for the impacted node and upload the collected tar file, once available. Attach the files to the fault report."
        ::= { eventGroup06 1 }

Usually the faulty process recovers from the error, but it could also be that some features may not work properly. Writing the core file itself may be service impacting. A continuous process failure may also escalate to a node restart.
The alarm is auto-deleted after some hours unless it is overwritten by a more recent core dump.
                            The problem can only be repaired by a SW correction. In order to collect debug information navigate to the log manager GUI and sort through the file collection directory for core dump files based on time stamp and process name. Upload the file.
Also run debug file collection for the impacted node and upload the collected tar file, once available. Attach the files to the fault report."
        ::= { eventGroup06 13 }

        alarm08003 NOTIFICATION-TYPE

                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            The node firewall has dropped outgoing IP packets and the number of dropped packets per minute has crossed a threshold. Dropping a packet may be:

(*) valid
(*) A SW error causing invalid packets to be sent
(*) A misconfigured node packet filter rule
(*) indicate a virus.
                            Use the mgmt node debug file collection function to upload debug files from the node that reported the alarm.

Analyze the dropped packets stored in the firewall log file to determine whether the IMP node sends invalid packets. If the packets are sent by valid IMP software escalate to development to either correct the packet filter rules or to modify the IMP SW not to send these packets.

If not, escalate to the next level of service to investigate whether there is a SW virus."

        --********************************************************************
        -- Alarm Trap Definitions for event group 58: Redis
        --********************************************************************

        alarm58001 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 58: Redis
                                eventName,                             -- 001: RedisClusterFail
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            Redis cluster is in fail state and can not recover by itself. As a result all requests to the data center is not being processed. Human intervention is needed immediately.
                            This alarm can occur during system startup and cluster formation. If this is not the case, check if all nodes are running. Check also if redis-cluster and redis-audit are running. If everything looks good then probably the cluster will not recover by itself. To recover the system lock all nodes (pmc state locked) then run '/etc/init.d/redis-audit clean' in all nodes, afterwards unlock the nodes (pmc state locked) - this way a fresh redis-cluster will start."
        ::= { eventGroup58 1 }

        alarm58002 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 58: Redis
                                eventName,                             -- 002: RedisClusterFailOver
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            One of the redis node is down so a failover just happened.
                            This alarm can happen temporarily if some other Access node is restarting. Please check if all nodes are running or if there are network issues. The redis audit will try to rebalance the cluster once the Access node is available again (then the alarm will be automatically cleared). The process of rebalancing can take about 5 to 15 minutes to complete."
        ::= { eventGroup58 2 }

        alarm58003 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 58: Redis

                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            A resharding is started, do not stop the nodes participating in the resharding until the alarm is cleared.
                            The redis audit is moving hash slots (resharding). This happens if nodes are added or removed, the alarm will be automatically cleared once the resharding process is complete. The process of resharding can take about 5 to 15 minutes to complete."
        ::= { eventGroup58 3 }

This alarm can also happen temporarily after resharding and rebalancing. The alarm will be automatically cleared once the cluster formation process is complete, this process can take about 5 minutes to complete."

                            Check faulty object to know where the problem is located."

        alarmC05005 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 05: ProcessManager
                                eventName,                             -- 005: RecoverEscalation
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                nodes,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            One or more process cannot be started.
If server Health State is 1 and the process continues to fail, all applicaton processes (Lvl 3) will be restarted.
If the HealthState is 2, the application restart did not work and all platform and all application processes (Lvl 1 and 2 will be restarted.
If the HealthState is 3, the node will be rebooted within 5 minutes.
                            Check which processe(s) are not working. Look for alarms reporting pstacks and coredumps. Collect debug files and send them to the next level of support for analysis."
        ::= { eventGroupC05 5 }


        --********************************************************************
        -- Alarm Trap Definitions for alarm eventC 06: CoreDump
        --********************************************************************

        alarmC06001 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 06: CoreDump
                                eventName,                             -- 001: PstackFound1
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                nodes,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            A pstack has been found. There was a severe SW error within the process/application specified in the faultyObject. Debugging information has been stored in the pstack file. Usually the faulty process recovers from the error, but it could also be that some features may not work properly. A continuous process failure may also escalate to a node restart.
The alarm is auto-deleted after some hours unless it is overwritten by a more recent core dump.
                            The problem can only be repaired by a SW correction. In order to collect debug information navigate to the log manager GUI and sort through the file collection directory for pstack files based on time stamp and process name. Upload the file.
Also run debug file collection for the impacted node and upload the collected tar file, once available. Attach the files to the fault report."
        ::= { eventGroupC06 1 }

                            The problem can only be repaired by a SW correction. In order to collect debug information navigate to the log manager GUI and sort through the file collection directory for core dump files based on time stamp and process name. Upload the file.
Also run debug file collection for the impacted node and upload the collected tar file, once available. Attach the files to the fault report."
        ::= { eventGroupC06 9 }

        alarmC08003 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 08: Security
                                eventName,                             -- 003: OutgoingPacketDropped
                                correlationId,
                                severity,
                                eventTime,
                                nodes,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            The node firewall has dropped outgoing IP packets and the number of dropped packets per minute has crossed a threshold. Dropping a packet may be:

(*) valid
(*) A SW error causing invalid packets to be sent
(*) A misconfigured node packet filter rule
(*) indicate a virus.
                            Use the mgmt node debug file collection function to upload debug files from the node that reported the alarm.

Analyze the dropped packets stored in the firewall log file to determine whether the IMP node sends invalid packets. If the packets are sent by valid IMP software escalate to development to either correct the packet filter rules or to modify the IMP SW not to send these packets.

If not, escalate to the next level of service to investigate whether there is a SW virus."
        ::= { eventGroupC08 3 }

        alarmC58001 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,
                                eventGroupName,                        -- 58: Redis
                                eventName,                             -- 001: RedisClusterFail

                                eventTime,
                                nodes,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            Redis cluster is in fail state and can not recover by itself. As a result all requests to the data center is not being processed. Human intervention is needed immediately.
                            This alarm can occur during system startup and cluster formation. If this is not the case, check if all nodes are running. Check also if redis-cluster and redis-audit are running. If everything looks good then probably the cluster will not recover by itself. To recover the system lock all nodes (pmc state locked) then run '/etc/init.d/redis-audit clean' in all nodes, afterwards unlock the nodes (pmc state locked) - this way a fresh redis-cluster will start."
        ::= { eventGroupC58 1 }

        alarmC58002 NOTIFICATION-TYPE
        OBJECTS        {        neName,
                                neType,

                                nodes,
                                faultyObject,
                                monitoredValue,
                                thresholdValues,
                                info   }
        STATUS                current
        DESCRIPTION        "Spontaneous Alarm from the managed network element:
                            One of the redis node is down so a failover just happened.
                            This alarm can happen temporarily if some other Access node is restarting. Please check if all nodes are running or if there are network issues. The redis audit will try to rebalance the cluster once the Access node is available again (then the alarm will be automatically cleared). The process of rebalancing can take about 5 to 15 minutes to complete."
        ::= { eventGroupC58 2 }

        ::= { eventGroupC58 3 }
